used for asynchronous I/O operations, while streams are used for synchronous I/O operations. Buffers, on the other hand, are used to handle fixed-size chunks of binary data. Streams are preferable when dealing with large files or continuous data, while buffers are suitable for smaller, fixed-size operations.</div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: rgb(145, 148, 172);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text">Buffers are only used for reading data, while streams are used for both reading and writing data. Buffers are preferable for real-time applications, while streams are suitable for batch processing.</div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div
